<p><b>Sven-Göran Eriksson</b> (<small>Swedish pronunciation: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Swedish" title="Help:IPA for Swedish">[ˈsvɛn ˈjœːˈran ˈeːrɪkˈsɔn]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata"> (<a href="/wiki/File:Sv-Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson.ogg" title="File:Sv-Sven-Göran Eriksson.ogg"><img alt="" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" width="13"/></a> <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a1/Sv-Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson.ogg" title="Sv-Sven-Göran Eriksson.ogg">listen</a>)</small>; born 5 February 1948) is a Swedish <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> <a href="/wiki/Coach_(sport)" title="Coach (sport)">manager</a> and former player, who is currently the manager of <a href="/wiki/China_League_One" title="China League One">China League One</a> side <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_F.C." title="Shenzhen F.C.">Shenzhen FC</a>.</p>
<p>As a manager, Eriksson won eighteen trophies with a variety of league clubs in Sweden, Portugal and Italy, between 1979 and 2000, and became the first manager to win <a href="/wiki/Double_(association_football)" title="Double (association football)">league-and-cup doubles</a> in three countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>He later managed the national teams of <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast_national_football_team" title="Ivory Coast national football team">Ivory Coast</a>, as well as three clubs in England. Eriksson has worked in nine countries: Sweden, Portugal, Italy, England, Mexico, Ivory Coast, Thailand, United Arab Emirates, and China.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Playing_career">Playing career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Playing career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Sunne,_Sweden" title="Sunne, Sweden">Sunne</a> and raised in <a href="/wiki/Torsby" title="Torsby">Torsby</a>, in <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A4rmland" title="Värmland">Värmland</a>. His father, also named Sven, was a bus conductor, and his mother, Ulla, worked in a textile store.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> He was nicknamed "<b>Svennis</b>" after his younger brother Lars-Erik's attempt to pronounce his name; Eriksson went on to become known by this nickname in Sweden.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-When_Saturdays_Comes_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-When_Saturdays_Comes-4">[4]</a></sup> He made his debut for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swedish_football_Division_4" title="Swedish football Division 4">Swedish football Division 4</a> team Torsby IF at the age of 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>He switched clubs to <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=SK_Sifh%C3%A4lla&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="SK Sifhälla (page does not exist)">SK Sifhälla</a> after moving to <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A4ffle" title="Säffle">Säffle</a> to study economics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> In 1972, he joined <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swedish_football_Division_2" title="Swedish football Division 2">Swedish football Division 2</a> team <a href="/wiki/KB_Karlskoga_FF" title="KB Karlskoga FF">KB Karlskoga FF</a>, where he also worked as a physical education teacher in <a href="/wiki/%C3%96rebro" title="Örebro">Örebro</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-invertingpyramid_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-invertingpyramid-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>He was heavily influenced by Karlskoga's player-manager, <a href="/wiki/Tord_Grip" title="Tord Grip">Tord Grip</a>, who favoured the English style of play that <a href="/wiki/Bob_Houghton" title="Bob Houghton">Bob Houghton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roy_Hodgson" title="Roy Hodgson">Roy Hodgson</a> had brought to the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-invertingpyramid_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-invertingpyramid-7">[7]</a></sup> Eriksson retired from playing in 1975 at the age of 27, after giving up on his dream of playing professional football; he summed up his brief playing career by saying "I was looked upon as a distinctly average defender, but someone who rarely made mistakes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Management_career">Management career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Management career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Degerfors_IF">Degerfors IF</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Degerfors IF">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Having retired as a player, Eriksson received an offer to become Tord Grip's assistant at <a href="/wiki/Degerfors_IF" title="Degerfors IF">Degerfors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-invertingpyramid_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-invertingpyramid-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> A year later, Grip was appointed assistant manager of the <a href="/wiki/Sweden_national_football_team" title="Sweden national football team">Sweden national team</a>, and Eriksson became Degerfors' manager. His stint as manager lasted from 1 January 1977 to 31 December 1978.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-degerforsjob_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-degerforsjob-10">[10]</a></sup> He led the team to the playoffs in 1977 and 1978, winning the latter and promotion to Swedish Football Division 2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-invertingpyramid_7-3"><a href="#cite_note-invertingpyramid-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IFK_G.C3.B6teborg">IFK Göteborg</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: IFK Göteborg">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>His success with assistant manager Tom Chadney by his side attracted the attention of much larger clubs, and Eriksson was appointed manager of <a href="/wiki/IFK_G%C3%B6teborg" title="IFK Göteborg">IFK Göteborg</a> on 1 January 1979.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goteborgjob_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-goteborgjob-11">[11]</a></sup> The move was such a surprise that many of the players had never even heard of him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-invertingpyramid_7-4"><a href="#cite_note-invertingpyramid-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>They finished second in <a href="/wiki/1978_Allsvenskan" title="1978 Allsvenskan">the Allsvenskan</a> and won the <a href="/wiki/Svenska_Cupen" title="Svenska Cupen">Svenska Cupen</a> for the first time in the club's history, defeating <a href="/wiki/%C3%85tvidabergs_FF" title="Åtvidabergs FF">Åtvidabergs FF</a> 6–1 in the final. Although results had improved, the team's style did not make him popular. He put results ahead of flair, emphasised tactical awareness and work rate, and he reined in the team's old cavalier style.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-invertingpyramid_7-5"><a href="#cite_note-invertingpyramid-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>As a consequence, the average attendance fell by 3,000 to 13,320.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-invertingpyramid_7-6"><a href="#cite_note-invertingpyramid-7">[7]</a></sup> Like Grip, he was influenced by Houghton and Hodgson and played a 4–4–2 with zonal marking and heavy pressing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-invertingpyramid_7-7"><a href="#cite_note-invertingpyramid-7">[7]</a></sup> Göteborg finished third in the <a href="/wiki/1980_Allsvenskan" title="1980 Allsvenskan">1980 season</a> and second again in <a href="/wiki/1981_Allsvenskan" title="1981 Allsvenskan">1981</a>. The following season, they won the <a href="/wiki/Treble_(association_football)" title="Treble (association football)">treble</a>. The team won the <a href="/wiki/1982_Allsvenskan" title="1982 Allsvenskan">League</a> and subsequent playoff, the Svenska Cupen, defeating <a href="/wiki/%C3%96sters_IF" title="Östers IF">Östers IF</a> 3–2 in the final.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Eriksson's international breakthrough came during the spring of 1982, when he led IFK Göteborg to the first ever <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Cup</a> for a Swedish club, defeating <a href="/wiki/Valencia_CF" title="Valencia CF">Valencia</a> in the quarter finals and <a href="/wiki/1._FC_Kaiserslautern" title="1. FC Kaiserslautern">1. FC Kaiserslautern</a> in the semi finals. Awaiting them in the <a href="/wiki/1982_UEFA_Cup_Final" title="1982 UEFA Cup Final">finals</a> was <a href="/wiki/Hamburger_SV" title="Hamburger SV">Hamburger SV</a>.</p>
<p>At <a href="/wiki/Ullevi" title="Ullevi">Ullevi</a> stadium in Gothenburg, Göteborg managed to score a late deciding goal, and took a 1–0 score with them to the away fixture, which they won 3–0, and with it, the <a href="/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_UEFA_Cup" title="1981–82 UEFA Cup">1981–82 UEFA Cup</a> by an aggregate score of 4–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> His club's success sparked interest in his skills from other clubs, leading him to leave IFK Göteborg in August 1982.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goteborgjob_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-goteborgjob-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Benfica">Benfica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Benfica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Eriksson's European success led to him being recruited by Portuguese club <a href="/wiki/S.L._Benfica" title="S.L. Benfica">Benfica</a>, which he joined on 1 September 1982.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-benficajob_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-benficajob-13">[13]</a></sup> Eriksson's influence was immediate, winning the <a href="/wiki/1982%E2%80%9383_Primeira_Divis%C3%A3o" title="1982–83 Primeira Divisão">Primeira Divisão</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%A7a_de_Portugal" title="Taça de Portugal">Taça de Portugal</a> and finishing runners-up in the <a href="/wiki/1982%E2%80%9383_UEFA_Cup" title="1982–83 UEFA Cup">1982–83 UEFA Cup</a> to <a href="/wiki/R.S.C._Anderlecht" title="R.S.C. Anderlecht">Anderlecht</a>. After winning a second consecutive <a href="/wiki/1983%E2%80%9384_Primeira_Divis%C3%A3o" title="1983–84 Primeira Divisão">league title</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Eriksson then moved on to Italy, becoming manager of <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">Roma</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-romajob_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-romajob-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roma">Roma</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Roma">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Eriksson joined Roma on 1 July 1984.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-romajob_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-romajob-15">[15]</a></sup> He was not as immediately successful at the <i>Giallorossi</i> as he had been before, but nonetheless still won a <a href="/wiki/Coppa_Italia" title="Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> with the club in 1986. Eriksson left the club on 6 May 1987.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-romajob_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-romajob-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fiorentina_and_return_to_Benfica">Fiorentina and return to Benfica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Fiorentina and return to Benfica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Eriksson was manager of <a href="/wiki/ACF_Fiorentina" title="ACF Fiorentina">Fiorentina</a> from 1 July 1987.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fiorentinajob_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-fiorentinajob-16">[16]</a></sup> Eriksson stint with the club was trophyless, and he moved back to Benfica for a second stint in 1989.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-benficajob_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-benficajob-13">[13]</a></sup> Eriksson led the Portuguese side to the <a href="/wiki/1990_European_Cup_Final" title="1990 European Cup Final">final</a> of the <a href="/wiki/1989%E2%80%9390_European_Cup" title="1989–90 European Cup">1989–90 European Cup</a> (losing to <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a> 1–0) in 1990, and another Primeira Divisão title in <a href="/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_Primeira_Divis%C3%A3o" title="1990–91 Primeira Divisão">1991</a>. Eriksson left the club in June 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-benficajob_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-benficajob-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sampdoria">Sampdoria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Sampdoria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In July 1992, Eriksson returned to Italy to lead <a href="/wiki/U.C._Sampdoria" title="U.C. Sampdoria">Sampdoria</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sampdoriajob_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-sampdoriajob-17">[17]</a></sup> where he managed to win another <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_Coppa_Italia" title="1993–94 Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> in 1994. He left in June 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sampdoriajob_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-sampdoriajob-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lazio">Lazio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Lazio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In December 1996, Eriksson agreed to leave Sampdoria at the end of the season, to manage <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> In February 1997, however, he went back on his word, and opted to stay in Italy and become the new manager at <a href="/wiki/S.S._Lazio" title="S.S. Lazio">Lazio</a>, effective 1 July 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-laziojob_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-laziojob-20">[20]</a></sup> Eriksson stated family reasons for wanting to stay in Italy, and Rovers would go on to appoint <a href="/wiki/Roy_Hodgson" title="Roy Hodgson">Roy Hodgson</a>.</p>
<p>Eriksson employed fellow Swede Tord Grip as his assistant. Eriksson finally found major success in Italy with Lazio when he won the <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_Coppa_Italia" title="1997–98 Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> and the Italian Supercup in 1998 and 2000, the <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_UEFA_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="1998–99 UEFA Cup Winners' Cup">European Cup Winners' Cup</a> (1999, the very last tournament), and the <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> title (the <i><a href="/wiki/Scudetto" title="Scudetto">Scudetto</a></i>) in <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_Serie_A" title="1999–2000 Serie A">2000</a> — only the second time that the Roman club had won the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Italian_football_champions" title="List of Italian football champions">Italian championship</a> in their history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="England_national_team">England national team</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: England national team">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In January 2001, Eriksson became the first foreign manager to take charge of the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England national team</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstforeignmanager_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-firstforeignmanager-22">[22]</a></sup> Throughout his five-year reign, of the 67 matches played, England won 40 games and lost 10. Almost immediately, he turned the team's fortunes around and they qualified top of <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_Group_9" title="2002 FIFA World Cup qualification – UEFA Group 9">Group 9</a> in <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">2002 FIFA World Cup</a> <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="2002 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">qualifying</a>. They qualified ahead of <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a>, and remained unbeaten after <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Keegan" title="Kevin Keegan">Kevin Keegan</a>'s side had lost to the Germans, in what was the last ever game at the original <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2002_World_Cup">2002 World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2002 World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Following the resignation of England manager Kevin Keegan after a home loss to Germany in October 2000, <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">The Football Association</a> (FA) pursued Eriksson as his replacement. Eriksson had initially agreed to take over after the expiration of his contract in June 2001, but decided to resign his post early at Lazio, and he officially began his England duties in January of that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-englandjob_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-englandjob-23">[23]</a></sup> Eriksson was the first foreign manager to be appointed coach of the England national team.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Eriksson turned around England's bid for qualification for the 2002 World Cup, with several crucial wins over lesser opposition, before his first real test — England's rematch with Germany in <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> on 1 September 2001. England crushed their <a href="/wiki/England%E2%80%93Germany_football_rivalry" title="England–Germany football rivalry">long-time rivals</a> <a href="/wiki/2001_Germany_v_England_football_match" title="2001 Germany v England football match">5–1</a>. Despite this, England still needed a late equaliser at home to <a href="/wiki/Greece_national_football_team" title="Greece national football team">Greece</a> to qualify automatically. At the finals, England drew with <a href="/wiki/Sweden_national_football_team" title="Sweden national football team">Sweden</a>, defeated their other longtime rivals <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a> 1–0, and drew with <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_national_football_team" title="Nigeria national football team">Nigeria</a> to qualify in second place from the four-team group. They went on to defeat <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team" title="Denmark national football team">Denmark</a> 3–0 in the Round of 16, before losing 2–1 to ten-man <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazil</a>, who went on to <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="2002 FIFA World Cup Final">win the tournament</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="UEFA_Euro_2004">UEFA Euro 2004</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: UEFA Euro 2004">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>After winning their first qualifying match in <a href="/wiki/Slovakia_national_football_team" title="Slovakia national football team">Slovakia</a>, England drew at home with <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_national_football_team" title="Macedonia national football team">Macedonia</a> and were then booed off by their fans after losing a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exhibition_match" title="Exhibition match">friendly</a> to <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_soccer_team" title="Australia national soccer team">Australia</a>. England, however, won their next five qualifiers and, needing a point from the last game to qualify, drew 0–0 in <a href="/wiki/Turkey_national_football_team" title="Turkey national football team">Turkey</a> to top the group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-englandqualifying_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-englandqualifying-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>In their first match in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2004" title="UEFA Euro 2004">finals</a>, England were winning 1–0 against <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France</a> after 90 minutes, but lost after <a href="/wiki/Zinedine_Zidane" title="Zinedine Zidane">Zinedine Zidane</a> scored twice in injury time. A 3–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_national_football_team" title="Switzerland national football team">Switzerland</a> and a 4–2 victory over <a href="/wiki/Croatia_national_football_team" title="Croatia national football team">Croatia</a>, however, meant England still qualified for a quarter-final against the hosts <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a>. There, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Owen" title="Michael Owen">Michael Owen</a> gave England an early lead only for <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A9lder_Postiga" title="Hélder Postiga">Hélder Postiga</a> to equalize. England then had a <a href="/wiki/Sol_Campbell" title="Sol Campbell">Sol Campbell</a> goal disallowed before ultimately losing on penalties.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2006_World_Cup">2006 World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2006 World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Regardless of the antipathy to Eriksson expressed by some in the English media, the England team professed total confidence in him, and in July 2004, threatened to strike during a media driven campaign to oust him. The FA renewed and extended Eriksson's contract by two further years to include <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2008" title="UEFA Euro 2008">UEFA Euro 2008</a>. On 7 September 2005, Eriksson's England team lost a World Cup qualifying match against <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Northern Ireland national football team">Northern Ireland</a> 1–0, the first time that England had lost to that team since 1972,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and one of only five competitive games lost during Eriksson's tenure.</p>
<p>Although it was England's first ever defeat in a World Cup or European Championship qualifying match under Eriksson, it brought his position under pressure and he was criticized, both by some fans and by commentators from the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Sport" title="BBC Sport">BBC</a>, for his alleged lack of charisma and tactical awareness. Criticism continued as England scraped a 1–0 victory over <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austrian_national_football_team" title="Austrian national football team">Austria</a>, in a game which saw <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a> controversially sent off. Some of the criticism from within the media was answered however, as England put in a much improved performance, despite the absence of Beckham through suspension and Sol Campbell and <a href="/wiki/Steven_Gerrard" title="Steven Gerrard">Steven Gerrard</a> through injury, in a 2–1 win against <a href="/wiki/Poland_national_football_team" title="Poland national football team">Poland</a>.</p>
<p>In January 2006, Eriksson was recorded saying he would be willing to leave England to manage <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> if England won the World Cup, after being duped into believing that a wealthy Arab would buy the club, and wanted him as manager. The wealthy "Arab" was in fact the "Fake Sheikh" <a href="/wiki/Mazher_Mahmood" title="Mazher Mahmood">Mazher Mahmood</a>, an undercover <i><a href="/wiki/News_of_the_World" title="News of the World">News of the World</a></i> reporter.</p>
<p>On 23 January, The FA announced that Eriksson would leave his job after the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 World Cup</a>, and it was thought that the <i>News of the World</i> allegations played a part in this decision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-englandsacking_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-englandsacking-25">[25]</a></sup> This was later denied by both parties, with Eriksson explaining that there was a prior arrangement to terminate his contract immediately after the World Cup.</p>
<p>In March 2006, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> reported that <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_national_football_team" title="South Africa national football team">South Africa</a> became the first potential employer publicly to register its interest in Eriksson.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> That job, however, went to <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Alberto_Parreira" title="Carlos Alberto Parreira">Carlos Alberto Parreira</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Tournament">The Tournament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: The Tournament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>England finished top of Group B at the finals, beating <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_national_football_team" title="Paraguay national football team">Paraguay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_national_football_team" title="Trinidad and Tobago national football team">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, before a 2–2 draw with Sweden, although the English press considered their performances far from satisfactory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the second round, a David Beckham trademark free kick was enough to see Eriksson's England past <a href="/wiki/Ecuador_national_football_team" title="Ecuador national football team">Ecuador</a> in a lacklustre 1–0 encounter affected by very high temperatures. Eriksson, however, once again fell to nemesis <a href="/wiki/Luiz_Felipe_Scolari" title="Luiz Felipe Scolari">Luiz Felipe Scolari</a>'s Portugal. They defeated England 3–1 on penalties with the score 0–0 after extra time, with Beckham lost to injury and <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Rooney" title="Wayne Rooney">Wayne Rooney</a> sent off for stamping on <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Carvalho" title="Ricardo Carvalho">Ricardo Carvalho</a>. The result was Eriksson's third successive exit in a major tournament quarter-final. In his farewell speech, Eriksson wished England well and singled out Rooney for special praise, advising the press not to blame the youngster's dismissal for England's exit.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Eriksson improved England's <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Rankings" title="FIFA World Rankings">FIFA World Rankings</a> place from seventeenth place in January 2001 to fifth in July 2006, reaching fourth during the 2006 World Cup, and was rated by The FA as England's second most successful manager after <a href="/wiki/Alf_Ramsey" title="Alf Ramsey">Alf Ramsey</a>. Under Eriksson, England achieved the highest point percentage in major tournament matches of all time for an England manager,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> losing only three competitive games (excluding extra time) and achieved top qualifying place in all three international tournaments.</p>
<p>In July 2006, after his final match with England, <a href="/wiki/ESPN_FC" title="ESPN FC">ESPN FC</a> reported he had turned down the chance to manage <a href="/wiki/Jamaica_national_football_team" title="Jamaica national football team">Jamaica</a>, as well as an unknown participating club in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> In October 2006, it was rumoured he was in talks to manage <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle</a>, in which his agent denied.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> In November 2006, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sun_(United_Kingdom)" title="The Sun (United Kingdom)">The Sun</a></i> reported that he was in secret talks to manage <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_national_football_team" title="Nigeria national football team">Nigeria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The job, however, ultimately went to <a href="/wiki/Berti_Vogts" title="Berti Vogts">Berti Vogts</a>, who lasted only thirteen months.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manchester_City">Manchester City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Manchester City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In July 2007, virtually a year to the day that he left the England job, Eriksson was confirmed as the new manager of <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> after signing a three-year contract worth £2 million per year, plus bonuses. He was City's first manager from outside the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manchestercityjob_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-manchestercityjob-32">[32]</a></sup> Before the season started, he signed striker <a href="/wiki/Rolando_Bianchi" title="Rolando Bianchi">Rolando Bianchi</a> for £8.8 million, along with midfielders <a href="/wiki/G%C3%A9lson_Fernandes" title="Gélson Fernandes">Gélson Fernandes</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geovanni_Deiberson_Maur%C3%ADcio" title="Geovanni Deiberson Maurício">Geovanni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Petrov" title="Martin Petrov">Martin Petrov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elano" title="Elano">Elano</a>; and defenders <a href="/wiki/Vedran_%C4%86orluka" title="Vedran Ćorluka">Vedran Ćorluka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Javier_Garrido" title="Javier Garrido">Javier Garrido</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>On 19 August, Manchester City beat <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_FA_Premier_League" title="2006–07 FA Premier League">reigning</a> <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> champions <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> to go top of the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Premier_League" title="2007–08 Premier League">2007–08 Premier League</a> after three games without conceding a goal. Eriksson received the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Manager_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Manager of the Month">Premier League's Manager of the Month</a> award for August. The club stayed in the top six throughout the rest of 2007, and were third throughout October and November, but fell to seventh on 12 January 2008 after winning only one of their previous five games.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In Spring 2008, Shinawatra claimed that he would replace Eriksson after only one full season due to an "avalanche of very poor results which is unacceptable at this level". In the last game of the season, Manchester City suffered an 8–1 loss to <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a>, the biggest defeat of Eriksson's career. Many concluded that the team had "gone on strike" as a symbolic protest during the game, although a <a href="/wiki/Penalty_card#Red_card" title="Penalty card">red card</a> for <a href="/wiki/Richard_Dunne" title="Richard Dunne">Richard Dunne</a> after 15 minutes made the game difficult for City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Manchester City ended in ninth place in the league, one place away from the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Cup</a> <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_UEFA_Cup_qualifying_rounds" title="2008–09 UEFA Cup qualifying rounds">2008–09 qualifying positions</a>. Manchester City subsequently qualified through the extra place awarded to the Premier League for finishing as the highest placed team who had not already qualified for a European competition in the UEFA Fair Play League for 2007–08.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Eriksson became the first Manchester City manager since <a href="/wiki/1969%E2%80%9370_Manchester_City_F.C._season" title="1969–70 Manchester City F.C. season">1969–70</a> to win both league derby games against Manchester United and also achieved the club's joint highest Premier League point total, 55.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>On 2 June 2008, Manchester City confirmed by club statement that they had parted company with Eriksson by "mutual consent", with Eriksson still having two years left on his contract. Following news of his departure, the City supporters' groups organised a petition with around 14,000 signatures which was handed to the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manchestercitysacking_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-manchestercitysacking-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico_national_team">Mexico national team</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Mexico national team">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 3 June 2008, Eriksson was officially signed to become manager of the <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico national team</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sven_takes_on_Mexico_post_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sven_takes_on_Mexico_post-35">[35]</a></sup> He formally started the role after Mexico's World Cup qualifier against <a href="/wiki/Belize_national_football_team" title="Belize national football team">Belize</a> on 21 June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> On 20 August 2008, he debuted as manager of Mexico in a <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF" title="CONCACAF">CONCACAF</a> <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(CONCACAF)" title="2010 FIFA World Cup qualification (CONCACAF)">World Cup qualifier</a> versus <a href="/wiki/Honduras_national_football_team" title="Honduras national football team">Honduras</a>. Mexico went on to win 2–1. On the next matches some results were poor, as Mexico tied with <a href="/wiki/Canada_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="Canada men's national soccer team">Canada</a> and lost to Jamaica and Honduras.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>On 11 February 2009, Eriksson was put under further pressure as his side lost 2–0 to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men's national soccer team">United States</a>. Calls for him to quit or be sacked were heard from the fans while English club <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a> were rumoured to be interested in making him their new manager. This link was strengthened by reports of members from the Portsmouth board flying to <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> to discuss contract offers with Eriksson and a possible compensation settlement with the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Football_Federation" title="Mexican Football Federation">Mexican Football Federation</a>.</p>
<p>On 3 March 2009, Eriksson continued to deny that he would leave Mexico and return to manage <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a>, insisting that he would remain and help Mexico qualify for the World Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> After a 3–1 World Cup qualifying loss at Honduras, Eriksson was removed as national team coach. Eriksson had only won one of his last seven non friendly games as manager.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mexicosacking_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-mexicosacking-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notts_County">Notts County</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Notts County">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 22 July 2009, Eriksson was appointed as <a href="/wiki/Director_of_football" title="Director of football">director of football</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Two" title="Football League Two">English League Two</a> team <a href="/wiki/Notts_County_F.C." title="Notts County F.C.">Notts County</a>, following that club's takeover by <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> consortium <a href="/wiki/Qadbak_Investments" title="Qadbak Investments">Munto Finance</a> with Eriksson getting a reported, but unconfirmed, £2 million per year deal. It is believed his contract was based on the future success of the club with a large percentage share holding making up his contract.</p>
<p>Eriksson later said that he was attracted by the consortium's plans to take the world's oldest league club to the top of the Premier League, and believed that they had the finance and commitment to do that. Large-scale investment in new facilities were promised, and Sol Campbell and <a href="/wiki/Kasper_Schmeichel" title="Kasper Schmeichel">Kasper Schmeichel</a> joined the club from Premier League teams. Campbell, however, played only one game before departing and Schmeichel was released at the end of the season.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>County's large debts, including an unpaid tax bill, emerged in November 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scott_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Scott-39">[39]</a></sup> On 11 February 2010, Eriksson resigned as director of football following the club's takeover by former <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_City_F.C." title="Lincoln City F.C.">Lincoln City</a> chairman <a href="/wiki/Ray_Trew" title="Ray Trew">Ray Trew</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Eriksson waived a multi-million payoff in order to assist the takeover, which chairman Trew described as the act of an "absolute gentleman". Notts County were promoted as League Two champions at the end of <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Football_League_Two" title="2009–10 Football League Two">the season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scott_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-Scott-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ivory_Coast_national_team">Ivory Coast national team</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ivory Coast national team">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 28 March 2010, Eriksson became the manager of the <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast_national_football_team" title="Ivory Coast national football team">Ivory Coast national team</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IvoryCoastjob_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-IvoryCoastjob-41">[41]</a></sup> Disclosure of the amount of money Eriksson's contract was worth has never been confirmed, but it has been reported that he received £270,000 for accepting the job. On 15 June, Ivory Coast played a 0–0 draw against Portugal in their opening game in <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_G" title="2010 FIFA World Cup Group G">Group G</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 World Cup finals</a>, followed by a 3–1 loss against Brazil on 20 June.</p>
<p>Despite defeating <a href="/wiki/North_Korea_national_football_team" title="North Korea national football team">North Korea</a> in the final group game 3–0, the Ivory Coast failed to qualify for the knockout stages. Prior to the match against Brazil, Brazilian coach <a href="/wiki/Dunga" title="Dunga">Dunga</a> commented, "With Eriksson, Ivory Coast has great balance. We used to see them play and they didn't have this type of organisation that they have now."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Svenleicestercity.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="688" data-file-width="303" height="386" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Svenleicestercity.png/170px-Svenleicestercity.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Svenleicestercity.png/255px-Svenleicestercity.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d8/Svenleicestercity.png 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Svenleicestercity.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Eriksson while manager of <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As there were no reported negotiations of an extension to Eriksson's contract between his agent and the <a href="/wiki/Ivorian_Football_Federation" title="Ivorian Football Federation">Ivorian Football Federation</a>, his contract ended on 25 June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IvoryCoastfarewell_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-IvoryCoastfarewell-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leicester_City">Leicester City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Leicester City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Eriksson was appointed manager of <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a> on 3 October 2010, as the Foxes sat in the relegation zone of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship" title="Football League Championship">Championship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sven-Goran_Eriksson_appointed_Leicester_City_manager_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sven-Goran_Eriksson_appointed_Leicester_City_manager-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> His first league game in charge resulted in a 1–1 draw against <a href="/wiki/Hull_City_A.F.C." title="Hull City A.F.C.">Hull City</a>, managed by <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Pearson" title="Nigel Pearson">Nigel Pearson</a> who had managed Leicester for the previous two seasons. This was quickly followed by Leicester's first victory under Eriksson, beating <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a> 2–1 at <a href="/wiki/Elland_Road" title="Elland Road">Elland Road</a>.</p>
<p>In December 2010, it was announced that Eriksson denied talks into becoming the new manager for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers" title="Blackburn Rovers">Blackburn Rovers</a>, following the exit of <a href="/wiki/Sam_Allardyce" title="Sam Allardyce">Sam Allardyce</a>, stating he was happy managing Leicester.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>Boosted by the loan signings of players such as <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Naughton" title="Kyle Naughton">Kyle Naughton</a> and later <a href="/wiki/Yakubu_Aiyegbeni" title="Yakubu Aiyegbeni">Yakubu</a>, results steadily improved under Eriksson as Leicester gradually began to climb the table, until a good run of form in the new year saw Leicester win seven of their first eight league games of 2011, and also take <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Premier_League" title="2010–11 Premier League">Premier League title</a> challengers and eventual cup winners Manchester City to a replay in the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_FA_Cup" title="2010–11 FA Cup">FA Cup</a>.</p>
<p>On 18 February 2011, after an injury time winner from <a href="/wiki/Martyn_Waghorn" title="Martyn Waghorn">Martyn Waghorn</a> at home to <a href="/wiki/Bristol_City_F.C." title="Bristol City F.C.">Bristol City</a>, Leicester had climbed to seventh in the table, and just one point off a play off place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Leicester's form, however, began to stutter as they won just two out of their following eleven games. The Foxes ended up finishing the season in 10th position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>Eriksson spent big in a bid for promotion in the summer of 2011, including multi-million pound transfer fees on <a href="/wiki/Matt_Mills" title="Matt Mills">Matt Mills</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jermaine_Beckford" title="Jermaine Beckford">Jermaine Beckford</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcwhandleic_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbcwhandleic-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> making them pre-season promotion favourites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcwhandleic_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbcwhandleic-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> After thirteen league matches, however, Eriksson left the club by mutual consent on 25 October 2011, with the Foxes sitting in the thirteenth position in the league, two points from a play-off position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leavesleicester_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-leavesleicester-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>Three players who were signed by Eriksson – Kasper Schmeichel, <a href="/wiki/David_Nugent" title="David Nugent">David Nugent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Konchesky" title="Paul Konchesky">Paul Konchesky</a> – were part of the Leicester team which won the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Football_League_Championship" title="2013–14 Football League Championship">2013–14 Championship</a> and survived relegation from the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Premier_League" title="2014–15 Premier League">2014–15 Premier League</a> under Nigel Pearson. Nugent credited Eriksson for his improved form at the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nugent_hails_Sven.27s_influence_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nugent_hails_Sven.27s_influence-54">[54]</a></sup> Of the three, Schmeichel was a key member of the first team that won the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Premier_League" title="2015–16 Premier League">2015–16 Premier League</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leicester_City:_Hard_workers_and_strong_characters_top_shopping_list_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Leicester_City:_Hard_workers_and_strong_characters_top_shopping_list-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Management_period">Management period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Management period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In an interview with <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Radio" title="Yorkshire Radio">Yorkshire Radio</a> on 8 February 2012, the chairman of Football League Championship club Leeds United, <a href="/wiki/Ken_Bates" title="Ken Bates">Ken Bates</a>, revealed that Eriksson had applied for the vacant managerial position at the club after the dismissal of <a href="/wiki/Simon_Grayson" title="Simon Grayson">Simon Grayson</a>. Bates went on to state that his application was unsuccessful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> On 3 September 2012, Eriksson was unveiled as the technical director of <a href="/wiki/BEC_Tero_Sasana_F.C." title="BEC Tero Sasana F.C.">BEC Tero Sasana</a>, a team in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thai_Premier_League" title="Thai Premier League">Thai Premier League</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 17 November 2012, Norwegian media reported that Eriksson was in talks with <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A5lerenga_Fotball" title="Vålerenga Fotball">Vålerenga</a>, about the possibility of taking over the soon to be available manager job for the <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a> based club. A meeting between the two parties was held on 21 November in Oslo, but no deal was made. In December, negotiations between Eriksson and the <a href="/wiki/Football_Federation_of_Ukraine" title="Football Federation of Ukraine">Football Federation of Ukraine</a>, who had offered him the position of head coach of the <a href="/wiki/Ukraine_national_football_team" title="Ukraine national football team">Ukraine national team</a>, did not bear fruit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KP261212FHUT_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-KP261212FHUT-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 6 January 2013, it was announced that Eriksson held talks about becoming the new manager for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers" title="Blackburn Rovers">Blackburn Rovers</a>, sixteen years after he nearly became the manager for the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> On 15 January 2013, it was announced that Eriksson would be joining German <a href="/wiki/2._Bundesliga" title="2. Bundesliga">2. Bundesliga</a> side <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TSV_1860_M%C3%BCnchen" title="TSV 1860 München">1860 Munich</a> as assistant to <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Schmidt_(football_manager)" title="Alexander Schmidt (football manager)">Alexander Schmidt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> On 18 January 2013, the club however reported, that Eriksson declined the offer to join 1860.</p>
<p>On 21 January 2013, Eriksson became technical director of <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>-based club <a href="/wiki/Al-Nasr_Dubai_SC" title="Al-Nasr Dubai SC">Al Nasr SC</a> in the <a href="/wiki/UAE_Arabian_Gulf_League" title="UAE Arabian Gulf League">UAE Arabian Gulf League</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson,_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="531" data-file-width="800" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson%2C_2014.jpg/220px-Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson%2C_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson%2C_2014.jpg/330px-Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson%2C_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson%2C_2014.jpg/440px-Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson%2C_2014.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson,_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Eriksson in China</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 4 June 2013, <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_R%26F_F.C." title="Guangzhou R&amp;F F.C.">Guangzhou R&amp;F</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Super_League" title="Chinese Super League">Chinese Super League</a> announced Eriksson as their new head coach, on an nineteen-month contract lasting until December 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> He was believed to be paid around £2 million a year for the job.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> He came up against former <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Marcello_Lippi" title="Marcello Lippi">Marcello Lippi</a> in the city's derby matches, as the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a> winner was manager of local rival <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Evergrande_F.C." title="Guangzhou Evergrande F.C.">Guangzhou Evergrande</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Under Eriksson, Guangzhou R&amp;F finished third in the league in 2014, and therefore qualified for the <a href="/wiki/AFC_Champions_League" title="AFC Champions League">AFC Champions League</a> for the first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> He left Guangzhou R&amp;F on 10 November 2014, after a disagreement in negotiations for extending his contract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>Eriksson signed a two-year contract with fellow Chinese Super League side <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shanghai_SIPG_F.C." title="Shanghai SIPG F.C.">Shanghai SIPG</a> on 18 November 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> He led Shanghai SIPG to finish runners up in the season of 2015, and qualified for the AFC Champions League for the first time.</p>
<p>Under Eriksson, Shanghai SIPG advanced to the quarter finals in their debut on the AFC Champions League, and guaranteed a seat of <a href="/wiki/2017_AFC_Champions_League" title="2017 AFC Champions League">2017 AFC Champions League</a> by finishing the third of the league in the 2016 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> However, Eriksson was criticized by single tactical play and failing to give chances to young talents throughout his term at SIPG.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> He was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Villas-Boas" title="André Villas-Boas">André Villas-Boas</a> on 4 November 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 5 December 2016, Eriksson became the manager of <a href="/wiki/China_League_One" title="China League One">China League One</a> side <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_F.C." title="Shenzhen F.C.">Shenzhen FC</a>, replacing <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Seedorf" title="Clarence Seedorf">Clarence Seedorf</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Eriksson's autobiography, <i>My Story</i>, was published in November 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> He married Ann-Christine Pettersson in July 1977.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2016, the house in which Eriksson lived in with Dell'Olio was put on the market for almost £4 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Eriksson purchased the house for £2,550,000 in July 2001, six months after he took over the national team of England. In 2003, he sold the house for £4,350,000.</p>
<p>In October 2016, Eriksson announced he was to take legal action against <a href="/wiki/Mazher_Mahmood" title="Mazher Mahmood">Mazher Mahmood</a>, the discredited undercover reporter for the now defunct tabloid newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/News_of_the_World" title="News of the World">News of the World</a></i>, as Mahmood's allegations led to Eriksson's contract termination as manager of England in January 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_seasons">List of seasons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: List of seasons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><b>LC</b> = League Cup</li>
<li><b>SC</b> = Super Cup</li>
<li><b>CL</b> = <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> (<i>European Cup prior to 1992</i>)</li>
<li><b>CWC</b> = <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="UEFA Cup Winners' Cup">UEFA Cup Winners' Cup</a> (<i>discontinued 1999</i>)</li>
<li><b>UC</b> = <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Cup</a> (<i>Now UEFA Europa League</i>)</li>
<li><b>USC</b> = <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Super_Cup" title="UEFA Super Cup">UEFA Super Cup</a></li>
</ul>
